< Text>
A lot of grass area for picnics, soccer, etc.  with tables including roof overhang in addition to a spacious playground.  The basketball court is still closed. Also, there is about a half-mile perimeter walkway that surrounds all these amenities which gives you an idea of this park's space.</Text>

< Text>
The park itself is nice enough. However, bring a can or two of raid. It is like a giant ant hill, and that is not an exaggeration. Additionally, there are some strange people there at night that are like vultures. They go unnoticed, but as soon as your party leaves the area, they swarm, digging through the trash and combing the area before you can even put your stuff away! It's a little unnerving. Just make sure you dont leave a purse or cell phone behind or it'll seriously be gone in seconds.</Text>

Once he was done he showed me how the door functions, how the one side (left) can stay shut and locked into place. I opted for the internal magnets and the standard nylon door handle.

Shawn left me with stickers to prevent people from walking through it and left me with a bottle of track silicone lube to make sure the screens keep moving smooth.

I am so happy I chose ClearView.

He answered my list of questions and it helped put my mind at ease.
I had my cyst removed and the surgery went well.  No complications and minimum discomfort post surgery.  I had my post op follow up appointments with Dr. Battaglia and his PA (Paul).
Thank you Dr. Battaglia and your staff.  I feel grateful and blessed for your excellent care .< /Text>

<rating>3<//rating>< Text>
I am an MBA student myself. In general and with all due respect, I consider the University of the People‚Äôs educational system as a self-learning one mainly because there are not examples to follow but instead  tasks to complete. Of course, these tasks are required with specific guidelines that help us understand what we need to produce. Although a reading section is provided, I would very much appreciate presentations from the instructors in a short video if not live well at least recorded. I have asked for these videos in every class and every term since I started because I think students deserve to be taught before being asked to preform. I began classes looking for a second degree, first degree from a large top tier research institution. Its a neat concept but they don't execute their own concept. <time>1596461186305</time><Rate>1</Rate><review>If you already hold a Bachelor's or Master's degree from a US school and you are looking for a second bachelor's degree, this school is not for you. If it's computer science, you are better off elsewhere. This school is for people who have no other means to get an education and rightfully so.
I hold a bachelor's and a master's degree in statistics and I was hoping to do their CS bachelors for fun and because it was cheaper but it's been a tug of war with their transfer policy.

I first enrolled with them when they did not accept transfer credits and I dropped out because they wanted to make me retake all the General Ed classes that I had already done from a regionally accredited school. Indeed that was a waste of time as I believed my time should be spent learning computer science courses like programming.

In the last couple of years, they've started accepting transfer credit and I reapplied again only to be given a lot of headaches. They make you take 5 foundational classes before you begin the CS program. I expected the foundational classes to be computer science classes but no. About 4 out of the 5 classes were general education classes which I intended to transfer.

I do not want to discuss my class experience in 2014, which was horrible BTW. It seems they still kept their peer evaluation which sucked.
Overall if you are in the US and you are looking for a second degree in CS, UoPeople is not the best route to go. I had to search google to find other regionally accredited online colleges where I could do my CS degree with about 75% credit transfer. Fort Hays gave me that.

UoPeople surely plays a role in educating people in/from poor and developing countries or countries where access to education is non-existent. It also plays a role in helping lower-class Americans, refugees, and asylum seekers get an affordable education. However, that is just as far as it goes. If you do not belong to any of these groups or you are a second-degree seeker with a RA degree, you are better off attending an online community college/college for CS. Their advisers were superb in replying to emails and that's the only positive. Furthermore, peer assessment helps prepare students for the workplace, where assessment by colleagues and constructive criticism are key components of professional development. < Text>
I will be done with my Associate Degree in Health Sciences by next year and University of the People is the best fit for me. The cost is affordable (it is tuition-free but there are exam processing fees to cover the university's costs), the learning is flexible, and most importantly, the curriculum is challenging and of high quality. I work part-time while studying, and I enjoy the autonomy and self-responsibility that comes with the degree program. And the courses are so challenging that I had to take 2 courses per term instead of 3 by my 2nd year. In my previous terms, peer-assessment was an issue but as I progress through my second year, I am encountering more thoughtful and constructive feedback that make me reflect on and improve my work. In summary, I recommend it for anyone who can take responsibility for his/her own work and who wants the flexibility and affordability of an fully-accredited American online degree< /Text>

<user_id>108688985658306678792< /user_id><name>sierra thomas</name><Date>1580948296678</Date><rate>5<//rate>< text>
REVIEW OF EDUCATION QUALITY/METHODS AND TOTAL COST OF ATTENDING UNIVERSITY OF THE PEOPLE:
Just to be clear, if you are looking for a stellar education, this is NOT IT!
You get minimal feedback from professors and the people largely responsible for grading your work are peers who know about as much (if not less) about the subject as you do.
Also, all materials are in text/video format, so if you're more of a hands-on learner, you might struggle a bit.

However, if you are looking for an affordable and flexible method of getting your basics out of the way so that you can move on to learning what you REALLY want to learn somewhere else, UoPeople is the place for you!

That being said, the tuition free model is definitely something that is worth perusing and UoPeople seems to be making it work well enough. So voting with your dollar for a good cause is definitely a plus.

Classes have a weekly deadline, but other than that, you can complete your course work on your own time. There are no scheduled skype sessions or timed group chats or scheduled final exams. If you can only complete your work at 3:00am, that's fine. If you can only squeeze in your classes on weekends, that's fine too. You complete the course work on YOUR TIME.

However, there is not a fast track option. Courses are only 8 weeks in length (so taking 2 classes is considered full time, 3 is over-time) so you still earn your degree at the same rate as any other university.

Also, they have gotten access to some really great textbooks (FOR FREE) that other colleges would make you pay $100+ for, so that's another advantage.

Bottom line, If you're a career person looking to further your education to enhance your understanding and performance in your profession, GO SOMEWHERE ELSE.
However, If you're a recent high school graduate who doesn't know what you want to do with your life and don't want to wrack up crippling debt for a degree you may or may not use/single mom who just needs that piece of paper to get a promotion/something along those lines, UNIVERSITY OF THE PEOPLE IS THE PLACE FOR YOU!

*PAYMENT INFORMATION*

P.S. a little information about what they mean by "FREE":
UoPeople is TUITION FREE. This does not mean that the entire education is free - you have a lot of professors, counselors, programmers, admin, etc. who all need to get paid for their time.
To cover this, expect to pay the following fees:
- $60 application fee:
this is very competitive as some universities charge up to $80-$100 application fees. Also, UoPeople doesn't seem to be too picky as to who they accept, so odds are that your application fee will earn you some results.
- $100 testing fee for every final you take:
This is a pay-as-you-go system, so it's not like you have to drop the money for classes you plan to take all at once. This fee is due at the end of the term, so you have about eight weeks to save back $100 per class. That being said, if you have to retake a class YOU WILL HAVE TO PAY THE TESTING FEE A SECOND TIME.
- Transfer fees:
If you are transferring credits you will have to pay a transfer fee. This fee seems to fluctuate based on how many credits you are transferring, but I was able to get 12 credit hours transferred for a $68 fee. Again, this is HIGHLY COMPETITIVE. They transferred every one of my credits that they possibly could, which was very helpful.
Other than that, I have not had to pay for a thing. The tuition is free, the counseling is free, and all of the reading/assignment materials are provided at no cost. Assuming I don't have to re-take a class, I will be able to earn an ASSOCIATES DEGREE FOR LESS THAN $2,600.00 and will not have to go into debt to do so.

THIS IS NOT A CHARITY CASE. THIS IS NOT A SCAM. IT IS A STARTING MODEL FOR TUITION-FREE EDUCATION. JUST KEEP IN MIND THAT THIS IS STILL A NEW MODEL AND THAT YOU GET WHAT YOU PAY FOR.< /text>

Being responsible not only for one's own learning but also for that of one's classmates increases commitment to study and enhances the experience. There is a lot to be gained from peer review, both from receiving and giving feedback. Because of a fake audience in reviews and promotions I have lost 60$ today .

They do provide a scholarship but there is no proof of evidence or promise to be given one.

Below is the detailed information of how much the University charges .

Hi,thanks for getting in touch. Please note that we are a tuition-free online university, as we do not charge our students for their educational instruction, course materials or annual enrollment. However, in order to ensure that our operations remain sustainable; we require that all applicants pay a one-time application processing fee of $60. Undergraduate students are also required to pay $100 per course as course assessment fee; while MBA/M.Ed. students are required to pay $200 per course as course assessment fee.
In order to complete an Associate‚Äôs degree, you will be required to pass 20 courses. Similarly, in order to complete a Bachelor‚Äôs degree, you will be required to pass 40 courses. As the course assessment fee is $100 USD per course, the expected total cost of the Associates program is $2,000 USD, and the Bachelor's program is $4,000 USD. Undergraduate students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $100 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.
In order to complete our MBA program, you will be required to pass 12 courses. As the course assessment fee is $200 USD per course, the expected total cost of the MBA program is $2,460 USD. MBA students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $200 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.
In order to complete our M.Ed. program, you will be required to pass 13 courses. As the course assessment fee is $200 USD per course, the expected total cost of the M.Ed. program is $2,660 USD. M.Ed. students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $200 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.< /Text>

<review>UoPeople review

UoPeople has helped open the door to a quality education that would otherwise remain closed. The Return on Investment is immense and the skills that you learn when you pursue your degree help you throughout your life. The University is just at its beginning stages, and once more people graduate from the University, more employers will recognize the degree. University of the People is in my opinion, one of the most valuable websites on the web. The most interesting thing about the college, in my opinion, is the fact that the advisory board consists of members of Ivy league colleges in the US, something that brings even more recognition to those who may be skeptical. I am very satisfied with my MBA degree process and when I am finished, I know I will look back and declare that it is one of the best decisions I've ever made in my life. UoPeople employs a Peer to Peer learning philosophy which further helps with learning uniquely. The important thing to realize is that you have an instructor that can modify any erroneous grades, so you are not at the mercy of an angry grader who scores your assignments :).  I am so happy that I found the MBA program at UoPeople and I cannot wait to see the University become more popular and prestigious.</review></record>
